class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n\t\t\t<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of Pacific hurricanes</h1>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">\n\t\t\t\t\tJump to:\t\t\t\t\t<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, \t\t\t\t\t<a href="#p-search">search</a>\n\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image">\n<div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div>\n</td>\n<td class="mbox-text">\n<div class="mbox-text-span">This article\'s <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute">factual accuracy</a> may be compromised due to out-of-date information</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small><i>(January 2013)</i></small></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>This is a <b>list of notable Pacific hurricanes</b>, subdivided by reason for <a href="/wiki/Notability" title="Notability">notability</a>. Notability means that it has met some criterion or achieved some statistic, or is part of a top ten for some superlative. It includes lists and rankings of <a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">Pacific hurricanes</a> by different characteristics and impacts.</p>\n<p>Characteristics include extremes of location, such as the northernmost or most equator-ward formation or position of a tropical cyclone. Other characteristics include its central pressure, windspeed, category on the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale">Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclogenesis" title="Tropical cyclogenesis">cyclogenesis</a> outside of a normal <a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">hurricane season\'s</a> timeframe, or storms that remain unnamed despite forming after tropical cyclone naming began in 1960. Another characteristic is how long a system went from formation to dissipation. These include the cost of damage, the number of casualties, as well as meteorological statistics such as <a href="/wiki/Rain" title="Rain">rainfall</a> point maxima.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Pauline_08_oct_1997_1849Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Hurricane_Pauline_08_oct_1997_1849Z.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Pauline_08_oct_1997_1849Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Hurricane_Pauline_08_oct_1997_1849Z.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Pauline_08_oct_1997_1849Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="600" /></a>\n<div <a href="/wiki/2001_Pacific_hurricane_season#Retirement" title="2001 Pacific hurricane season">Israel</a> were removed from the list of names during and after the 2001 season due to political sensitivities. <a href="/wiki/1987_Pacific_hurricane_season#Tropical_Storm_Knut" title="1987 Pacific hurricane season">Knut</a> was removed from the list in 1988 for unknown reasons. <a href="/wiki/1970_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Adele" title="1970 Pacific hurricane season">Adele</a>, <a href="/wiki/1988_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Iva" title="1988 Pacific hurricane season">Iva</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Fefa_(1991)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Fefa (1991)">Fefa</a> were also removed in 1970, 1988, and 1991 respectively for unknown reasons. <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Hazel_(1965)" title="Tropical Storm Hazel (1965)">Hazel</a> was replaced in 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-Adolph_retirement_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adolph_retirement-1">[1]</a></sup> The name <a href="/wiki/2004_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Isis" title="2004 Pacific hurricane season">Isis</a> was also pre-emptively removed from the lists of names for 2016 after being deemed inappropriate because of the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">eponymous militant group</a> in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-retired_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-retired-2">[2]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unnamed_but_historically_significant">Unnamed but class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Seasonal activity and records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Central_Pacific_Hurricane_Center" title="Central Pacific Hurricane Center">Central Pacific Hurricane Center</a>\'s (CPHC) <a href="/wiki/Area_of_responsibility" title="Area of responsibility">area of responsibility</a> (AOR), the season with the most tropical cyclones is the <a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2015 Pacific hurricane season">2015</a> season with 16 cyclones forming in or entering the region. A season without cyclones has happened a few times since 1966, most recently in <a href="/wiki/1979_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1979 Pacific hurricane season">1979</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CPHC_all_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPHC_all-30">[30]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Highest">Highest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/1992_Pacific_hurricane_season_summary.jpg/330px-1992_Pacific_hurricane_season_summary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/1992_Pacific_hurricane_season_summary.jpg/440px-1992_Pacific_hurricane_season_summary.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1796" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1992_Pacific_hurricane_season_summary.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nTrack map of the <a season</a></th>\n<td>20</td>\n<td>16</td>\n<td>6</td>\n<td>1</td>\n<td>0</td>\n<td>0</td>\n<td>21</td>\n<td>16</td>\n<td>6</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lowest">Lowest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Lowest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Before 1971 and especially 1966, data in this basin is extremely unreliable. The geostationary satellite era began in 1966,<sup id="cite_ref-Rhome_Brown_Mainelli_Blake_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rhome_Brown_Mainelli_Blake-31">[31]</a></sup> and that year is often considered the first year of reliable tropical records.<sup id="cite_ref-Padgett_August_2000_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Padgett_August_2000-32">[32]</a></sup> Intensity estimates are most reliable starting in the 1971 season. A few years later, the <a href="/wiki/Dvorak_technique" title="Dvorak technique">Dvorak technique</a> came into use. Those two factors make intensity estimates more reliable starting in that year.<sup id="cite_ref-Padgett_August_2000_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Padgett_August_2000-32">[32]</a></sup> For these reasons, seasons prior to 1971 are not included.</p>\n<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">\n<tr>\n<th scope="col" rowspan="2">Year</th>\n<th scope="col" colspan="3">NHC\'s AOR</th>\n<th />\nhurricanes</th>\n<th scope="col">Tropical<br />\nstorms</th>\n<th scope="col">Hurricanes</th>\n<th scope="col">Major<br />\nhurricanes</th>\n<th scope="col">Tropical<br />\nstorms</th>\n<th href="/wiki/1995_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1995 Pacific hurricane season">1995 history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Naming history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oho_2015-10-06_2310Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Oho_2015-10-06_2310Z.jpg/220px-Oho_2015-10-06_2310Z.jpg" width="220" height="291" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Oho_2015-10-06_2310Z.jpg/330px-Oho_2015-10-06_2310Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Oho_2015-10-06_2310Z.jpg/440px-Oho_2015-10-06_2310Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5681" data-file-height="7521" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oho_2015-10-06_2310Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Oho" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Oho">Hurricane Oho</a>, the eighth system to receive a central Pacific name in 2015</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Naming of tropical cyclones in the eastern north Pacific began in the <a href="/wiki/1950-1969_Pacific_hurricane_seasons#1960_Season" class="mw-redirect" title="1950-1969 Pacific hurricane seasons">1960 season</a>. That year, four lists of names were created. The plan was to proceed in a manner similar to that of the western Pacific; that is, the name of the first storm in one season would be the next unused one from the same list, and when the bottom of one list was reached the next list was started. This scheme was abandoned in 1965 and next year, the lists started being recycled on a four-year rotation, starting with the A name each year.<sup id="cite_ref-ATWC_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATWC-33">[33]</a></sup> That same general scheme remains in use today, although the names and lists are different. On average, the eastern north Pacific sees about sixteen named storms per year.<sup id="cite_ref-NCDC_2006_summary_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCDC_2006_summary-34">[34]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Named_storms_per_month">Named storms per month</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Named storms per month">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Darby,_Estelle,_Frank_and_Eight_2016-07-22_0000Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Darby%2C_Estelle%2C_Frank_and_Eight_2016-07-22_0000Z.jpg/250px-Darby%2C_Estelle%2C_Frank_and_Eight_2016-07-22_0000Z.jpg" width="250" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Darby%2C_Estelle%2C_Frank_and_Eight_2016-07-22_0000Z.jpg/375px-Darby%2C_Estelle%2C_Frank_and_Eight_2016-07-22_0000Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Darby%2C_Estelle%2C_Frank_and_Eight_2016-07-22_0000Z.jpg/500px-Darby%2C_Estelle%2C_Frank_and_Eight_2016-07-22_0000Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="17072" data-file-height="9336" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Darby,_Estelle,_Frank_and_Eight_2016-07-22_0000Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nFour of the July <a href="/wiki/Cyclone" title="Cyclone">cyclones</a> during the 2016 season</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Before 1971 and especially 1966, data in this basin is extremely unreliable. The geostationary satellite era began in 1966,<sup id="cite_ref-Rhome_Brown_Mainelli_Blake_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rhome_Brown_Mainelli_Blake-31">[31]</a></sup> and that year is often considered the first year of reliable tropical records.<sup id="cite_ref-Padgett_August_2000_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Padgett_August_2000-32">[32]</a></sup> Intensity estimates are more reliable starting in the 1971 season. A few years later, the <a href="/wiki/Dvorak_technique" title="Dvorak technique">Dvorak technique</a> came into use. Those two make intensity estimates more reliable starting in that year.<sup id="cite_ref-Padgett_August_2000_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Padgett_August_2000-32">[32]</a></sup> For these reasons, seasons before 1966 are not included in the lowest column.</p>\n<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">\n<tr>\n<th scope="col" rowspan="2">Month</th>\n<th colspan="2">Most Source:<sup id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Off-season_storms">Off-season storms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Off-season storms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_off-season_Pacific_hurricanes" title="List of off-season Pacific hurricanes">List of off-season Pacific hurricanes</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ekeka_feb_2_1992_0221Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Ekeka_feb_2_1992_0221Z.jpg/220px-Ekeka_feb_2_1992_0221Z.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Ekeka_feb_2_1992_0221Z.jpg/330px-Ekeka_feb_2_1992_0221Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Ekeka_feb_2_1992_0221Z.jpg/440px-Ekeka_feb_2_1992_0221Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="601" data-file-height="601" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ekeka_feb_2_1992_0221Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA meteorological enigma, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ekeka" title="Hurricane Ekeka">Hurricane Ekeka</a> formed in January and became a major hurricane.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The Pacific hurricane season runs from May 15 to November 30.<sup id="cite_ref-season_dates_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-season_dates-36">[36]</a></sup> Only systems that develop or enter during the off-season are included. The earliest off-season storm is Pali in 2016 whilst the latest off-season storm was Nine-C during 2015.</p>\n<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">\n<tr>\n<th scope="col">Name</th>\n<th season">Adrian</a></th>\n<td>May 9, 2017</td>\n<td></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>\xe2\x80\xa0Entered the basin on this date</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Unnamed_storms">Unnamed storms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Unnamed storms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_unnamed_tropical_cyclones" title="List of unnamed tropical cyclones">List of unnamed tropical cyclones</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Unnamed_Hurricane_(1975).PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Unnamed_Hurricane_%281975%29.PNG/220px-Unnamed_Hurricane_%281975%29.PNG" width="220" height="251" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Unnamed_Hurricane_%281975%29.PNG/330px-Unnamed_Hurricane_%281975%29.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Unnamed_Hurricane_%281975%29.PNG/440px-Unnamed_Hurricane_%281975%29.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1703" data-file-height="1940" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Unnamed_Hurricane_(1975).PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe unnamed hurricane of 1975 near the Pacific Northwest</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Tropical cyclones have received official names in the east-central Pacific region since 1960. Since this time, 5 systems that have formed in this area have not received a name, plus another possible <a href="/wiki/2006_central_Pacific_cyclone" class="mw-redirect" title="2006 central Pacific cyclone">unnamed subtropical or tropical system</a> in 2006.</p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/1962_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1962 Pacific hurricane season">Tropical Storm 4&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 1962</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/1962_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1962 Pacific hurricane season">Tropical Storm 8&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 1962</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/1963_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1963 Pacific hurricane season">Tropical Storm 4&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 1963</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/1975_Pacific_Northwest_hurricane" title="1975 Pacific Northwest hurricane">Hurricane 12&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 1975</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/1996_Pacific_hurricane_season#Tropical_Storm_One-E" title="1996 Pacific hurricane season">Tropical Storm 1&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 1996</a></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Strength">Strength</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Strength">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span 2x" data-file-width="32" data-file-height="28" /> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Tropical_cyclones" title="Portal:Tropical cyclones">Tropical cyclones portal</a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n</div>\n<p>Since 1959, only 15 Pacific hurricanes are known to have reached Category&#160;5 and none made landfall while at this intensity.<sup id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_35-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Category_4">Category 4</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Category 4">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_4_Pacific_hurricanes" title="List of Category 4 Pacific hurricanes">List of Category 4 Pacific hurricanes</a></div>\n<p>Since 1900, 113&#160;Pacific hurricanes have attained Category&#160;4 intensity, of which four made landfall at that strength.<sup id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_35-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Duration_records">Duration records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Duration records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tina_30_September_1992.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Tina_30_September_1992.png/220px-Tina_30_September_1992.png" width="220" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Tina_30_September_1992.png/330px-Tina_30_September_1992.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Tina_30_September_1992.png/440px-Tina_30_September_1992.png 2x" data-file-width="575" data-file-height="601" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tina_30_September_1992.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Tina_(1992)" title="Hurricane Tina (1992)">Hurricane Tina</a>, the longest lasting Pacific hurricane east of the international dateline</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>This lists all Pacific hurricanes that existed as tropical cyclones while in the Pacific Ocean east of <a href="/wiki/180th_meridian" title="180th meridian">the dateline</a> for more than two weeks continuously. Hurricanes John and Dora spent some time in the west Pacific before dissipating. John spent eleven days west of the dateline; if that time was included John would have existed for a total of 30&#160;days and 18&#160;hours, a world record, while including Dora\'s time in the west Pacific would mean that it existed for 18 days.<sup id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_35-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-35">[35]</a></sup> One Atlantic hurricane, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Joan-Miriam" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Joan-Miriam">Hurricane Joan</a>, crossed into this basin and was renamed Miriam,<sup id="cite_ref-E15_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-E15-45">[45]</a></sup> giving it a total lifespan of 22&#160;days,<sup id="cite_ref-HURDAT_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-46">[46]</a></sup> but not all of that was in the Pacific. 1993\'s Greg formed from the remnants of <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bret_(1993)" title="Tropical Storm Bret (1993)">1993\'s Tropical Storm Bret</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-E15_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-E15-45">[45]</a></sup> Its time as an Atlantic system is excluded.</p>\n<p>All of these systems except Trudy, Olaf, and Connie existed in both the east and central Pacific, and all except Olaf were hurricanes. Hurricane Trudy of 1990 is thus the longest lived eastern Pacific hurricane to stay in the eastern Pacific. Tropical Storm Olaf of 1997 is hence the longest-lived eastern Pacific tropical cyclone <i>not</i> to reach hurricane intensity.<sup id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_35-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<p>No known tropical cyclone forming in the central north Pacific lasted for longer than 14&#160;days without crossing into <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_basins" title="Tropical cyclone basins">another basin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_35-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-35">[35]</a></sup> The tropical cyclone forming in the central Pacific that spent the most time there was <a href="/wiki/2014_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Ana" title="2014 Pacific hurricane season">2014\'s Hurricane Ana</a> at 12.75&#160;days from formation to extratropical transition.<sup id="cite_ref-AnaTCR_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnaTCR-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tc_records_CPHC_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tc_records_CPHC-48">[48]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">\n<tr>\n<th scope="col">Rank</th>\n<th rowspan="3">15</th>\n<td>14.00</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1990_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Marie" title="1990 Pacific hurricane season">Marie</a></td>\n<td>1990</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>14.00</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1993_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Greg" title="1993 Pacific hurricane season">Greg</a></td>\n<td>1993</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>14.00</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dora_(1999)" title="Hurricane Dora (1999)">Dora</a></td>\n<td>1999</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Before the <a href="/wiki/Weather_satellite" title="Weather satellite">weather satellite</a> era began, the lifespans of many Pacific hurricanes may be underestimated.<sup id="cite_ref-Padgett_August_2000_32-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Padgett_August_2000-32">[32]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Crossover_storms">Crossover storms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Crossover storms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="From_Atlantic_to_Eastern_Pacific">From Atlantic to Eastern Pacific</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: From Atlantic to Eastern Pacific">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Atlantic%E2%80%93Pacific_crossover_hurricanes" title="List of Atlantic\xe2\x80\x93Pacific crossover hurricanes">List of Atlantic\xe2\x80\x93Pacific crossover hurricanes</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tracks_of_Atlantic-Pacific_crossover_storms.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tracks_of_Atlantic-Pacific_crossover_storms.png/220px-Tracks_of_Atlantic-Pacific_crossover_storms.png" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tracks_of_Atlantic-Pacific_crossover_storms.png/330px-Tracks_of_Atlantic-Pacific_crossover_storms.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tracks_of_Atlantic-Pacific_crossover_storms.png/440px-Tracks_of_Atlantic-Pacific_crossover_storms.png 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="633" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tracks_of_Atlantic-Pacific_crossover_storms.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nTracks of Atlantic-Pacific crossovers on both directions</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>This includes only systems which stayed a tropical cyclone during the passage or that maintained a circulation during the crossover.</p>\n<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">\n<tr>\n<th scope="col">Season</th>\n<th scope="col">Storm (Atlantic)</th>\n<th scope="col">Storm (Pacific)</th>\n<th scope="col"><abbr hurricane season">Unnumbered tropical depression</a></td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row"><a class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/1996_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1996 Pacific hurricane season">1996</a></th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Cesar%E2%80%93Douglas" title="Hurricane Cesar\xe2\x80\x93Douglas">Cesar</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Cesar%E2%80%93Douglas" title="Hurricane Cesar\xe2\x80\x93Douglas">Douglas</a></td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-Douglas_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Douglas-57">[57]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/2016_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2016 Pacific hurricane season">2016</a></th>\n<td colspan="2">\n<div style="text-align: center;"><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Otto" title="Hurricane Otto">Otto</a></div>\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-Otto_-_Adv_17_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Otto_-_Adv_17-58">[58]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>It used to be that when a Pacific named storm crossed North America and made it to the Atlantic (or vice versa), it would receive the next name on the respective basin\'s list. However, in 2000 this policy was changed so that a tropical cyclone will keep its name if it remains a tropical cyclone during the entire passage. Only if it dissipates and then re-forms does it get renamed.<sup id="cite_ref-b5_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b5-59">[59]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="From_Eastern_Pacific_to_Atlantic">From Eastern Pacific to Atlantic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: From Eastern Pacific to Atlantic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Atlantic%E2%80%93Pacific_crossover_hurricanes" title="List of Atlantic\xe2\x80\x93Pacific crossover hurricanes">List of Atlantic\xe2\x80\x93Pacific crossover hurricanes</a></div>\n<p>This includes only systems which stayed a tropical cyclone during the passage or that maintained a circulation during the crossover.</p>\n<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">\n<tr>\n<th scope="col">Season</th>\n<th scope="col">Storm (Pacific)</th>\n<th to those, there are apparently two additional ones. One existed before 1856 and made it to the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hurd_p_47_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hurd_p_47-65">[65]</a></sup> Another Pacific tropical cyclone crossed over central Mexico and also made it to the Gulf sometime after September 9, 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-Hurd_p_47_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hurd_p_47-65">[65]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="From_Eastern_Pacific_to_Western_Pacific">From Eastern Pacific to Western Pacific</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: From Eastern Pacific to Western Pacific">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Genevieve_Aug_06_2014_2245Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Genevieve_Aug_06_2014_2245Z.jpg/170px-Genevieve_Aug_06_2014_2245Z.jpg" width="170" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Genevieve_Aug_06_2014_2245Z.jpg/255px-Genevieve_Aug_06_2014_2245Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Genevieve_Aug_06_2014_2245Z.jpg/340px-Genevieve_Aug_06_2014_2245Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6400" data-file-height="8400" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Genevieve_Aug_06_2014_2245Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n2014\'s <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Genevieve_(2014)" title="Hurricane Genevieve (2014)">Hurricane Genevieve</a> existed in all three north Pacific tropical cyclone basins</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Neither eastern Pacific tropical cyclones passing 140\xc2\xb0W, nor central Pacific tropical cyclones crossing the dateline, are notable events. However, very few eastern Pacific proper cyclones that enter the central Pacific make it to the dateline.</p>\n<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">\n<tr>\n<th scope="col">Name</th>\n<th Hurricane Li formed in the eastern Pacific, but was not named until it crossed into the central Pacific.</p>\n<p>In addition, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jimena_(2003)" title="Hurricane Jimena (2003)">Hurricane Jimena</a> of <a href="/wiki/2003_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2003 Pacific hurricane season">2003</a> is recognized per <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">NHC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Pacific_Hurricane_Center" title="Central Pacific Hurricane Center">CPHC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">JTWC</a> as a storm that existed in all three areas of responsibility, but isn\'t recognized by the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">JMA</a> as a official western Pacific tropical cyclone.<sup id="cite_ref-NHC_Jimena_report_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHC_Jimena_report-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CPHC_Rebest_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPHC_Rebest-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JMA_BT_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JMA_BT-74">[74]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="From_Western_Pacific_to_Central_Pacific">From Western Pacific to Central Pacific</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: From Western Pacific to Central Pacific">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_John_23_aug_1994_1739Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Hurricane_John_23_aug_1994_1739Z.jpg/170px-Hurricane_John_23_aug_1994_1739Z.jpg" width="170" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Hurricane_John_23_aug_1994_1739Z.jpg/255px-Hurricane_John_23_aug_1994_1739Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Hurricane_John_23_aug_1994_1739Z.jpg/340px-Hurricane_John_23_aug_1994_1739Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="540" data-file-height="608" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_John_23_aug_1994_1739Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n1994\'s <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_John_(1994)" title="Hurricane John (1994)">Hurricane John</a> crossed the dateline twice, from the central to the western Pacific and back</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Tropical cyclones crossing from the western Pacific to the central Pacific are fairly rare, and this has happened only seven times before. Of those seven times, five of them were storms which crossed the dateline twice; from the western to the central pacific and back (or vice versa). No tropical cyclone from the western Pacific has ever made it past 140\xc2\xb0W.</p>\n<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">\n<tr>\n<th scope="col">Name</th>\n<th scope="col">Season</th>\n<th John formed in the eastern Pacific.</p>\n<p>In addition, <a href="/wiki/1958_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_June" title="1958 Pacific hurricane season">Typhoon June</a> of <a href="/wiki/1958_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1958 Pacific hurricane season">1958</a> and <a href="/wiki/2000_Pacific_hurricane_season#Tropical_Storm_Wene" title="2000 Pacific hurricane season">Tropical Storm Wene</a> of <a href="/wiki/2000_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2000 Pacific hurricane season">2000</a> are recognized per <a href="/wiki/Central_Pacific_Hurricane_Center" title="Central Pacific Hurricane Center">CPHC</a> as basin-crossing storms, but aren\'t recognized as such by the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">JMA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1958WBH_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1958WBH-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CPHC_2000_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPHC_2000-82">[82]</a></sup> Also, <a href="/wiki/1984_Pacific_hurricane_season#Tropical_Storm_Moke" title="1984 Pacific hurricane season">Tropical Storm Moke</a> of <a href="/wiki/1984_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1984 Pacific hurricane season">1984</a> may have achieved this feat as well, however it isn\'t recognized as an official western Pacific tropical cyclone by either the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">JMA</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">JTWC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CPHC_Rebest_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPHC_Rebest-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JMA_BT_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JMA_BT-74">[74]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="From_Central_Pacific_to_Eastern_Pacific">From Central Pacific to Eastern Pacific</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: From Central Pacific to Eastern Pacific">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ulika_2016-09-27_2325Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Ulika_2016-09-27_2325Z.jpg/170px-Ulika_2016-09-27_2325Z.jpg" width="170" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Ulika_2016-09-27_2325Z.jpg/255px-Ulika_2016-09-27_2325Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Ulika_2016-09-27_2325Z.jpg/340px-Ulika_2016-09-27_2325Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1872" data-file-height="2392" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ulika_2016-09-27_2325Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n2016\'s <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ulika" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Ulika">Hurricane Ulika</a> crossed 140\xc2\xb0W thrice, moving from the eastern to the central Pacific twice</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Tropical cyclones crossing from the eastern Pacific to the central Pacific are routine; ones going the other way are not. That event has happened thrice.</p>\n<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">\n<tr>\n<th scope="col">Name</th>\n<th scope="col">Season</th>\n<th scope="col"><abbr title="Reference">Ref.</abbr></th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/1982_Pacific_hurricane_season#Tropical_Storm_Ema" title="1982 Pacific hurricane season">Ema</a></th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1982_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1982 Pacific hurricane season">1982</a></td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_35-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-35">[35]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Olaf" title="2015 Pacific hurricane season">Olaf</a><img alt="dagger" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9" height="14" data-file-width="9" data-file-height="14" /></th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2015 Pacific hurricane season">2015</a></td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/2016_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Ulika" title="2016 Pacific hurricane season">Ulika</a><img alt="dagger" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9" height="14" data-file-width="9" data-file-height="14" /></th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/2016_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2016 Pacific hurricane season">2016</a></td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p><img alt="dagger" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9" height="14" data-file-width="9" data-file-height="14" /> System crossed 140\xc2\xb0W more than once.</p>\n<p>It was previously believed that an <a href="/wiki/Unnamed_Hurricane_(1975)" class="mw-redirect" title="Unnamed Hurricane (1975)">Unnamed Hurricane</a> of <a href="/wiki/1975_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1975 Pacific hurricane season">1975</a> crossed 140\xc2\xb0W and is still included in the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">NHC</a> as such, but according to a reanalysis made by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Pacific_Hurricane_Center" title="Central Pacific Hurricane Center">CPHC</a> the storm became extratropical before doing so.<sup id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_35-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CPHC_Rebest_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPHC_Rebest-73">[73]</a></sup> In addition, an <a href="/wiki/2006_central_Pacific_cyclone" class="mw-redirect" title="2006 central Pacific cyclone">unofficial cyclone</a> formed on October 30, 2006 in the central Pacific subtropics. It eventually developed an <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye-like</a> structure.<sup id="cite_ref-NASA-91C_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-91C-85">[85]</a></sup> Its track data indicates that it crossed from the central to the east Pacific because it formed at longitude 149\xc2\xb0W and dissipated at 135\xc2\xb0W.<sup id="cite_ref-Padgett_tracks_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Padgett_tracks-86">[86]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>, which is not a meteorological organization, called this system a <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_cyclone" title="Subtropical cyclone">subtropical cyclone</a>, and the Naval Research Laboratory Monterey had enough interest in it to call it 91C.<sup id="cite_ref-NASA-91C_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-91C-85">[85]</a></sup> The system has also been called <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CHC_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHC-87">[87]</a></sup> This cyclone is unofficial because it is not included in the seasonal reports of either <a href="/wiki/Regional_Specialized_Meteorological_Center" title="Regional Specialized Meteorological Center">Regional Specialized Meteorological Center</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CPHC_2006_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPHC_2006-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NHC_2006_archive_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHC_2006_archive-89">[89]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Intensity_records">Intensity records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Intensity records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ten_most_intense">Ten most intense</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Ten most intense">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Patricia_2015-10-23_1730Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Patricia_2015-10-23_1730Z.jpg/220px-Patricia_2015-10-23_1730Z.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Patricia_2015-10-23_1730Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Patricia" title="Hurricane Patricia">Hurricane Patricia</a>, the most intense Pacific hurricane on record</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Per_lowest_central_pressure">Per lowest central pressure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Per lowest central pressure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The apparent increase in recent seasons is spurious; it is due to better estimation and measurement, not an increase in intense storms. That is, until 1988, Pacific hurricanes generally did not have their central pressures measured or estimated from satellite imagery.</p>\n<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">\n<tr>\n<th id="Strongest_storm_in_each_month">Strongest storm in each month</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Intensity is measured solely by central pressure unless the pressure is not known, in which case intensity is measured by maximum sustained class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Unusual landfall locations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="California">California</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: California">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_California_hurricanes" title="List of California hurricanes">List of California hurricanes</a></div>\n<ul>\n<li><b>After October or before June, 1854</b>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 A system considered a tropical cyclone makes landfall just north of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gate" title="Golden Gate">Golden Gate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Visher_p296_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Visher_p296-60">[60]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Late September, early October 1858</b>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 A <a href="/wiki/1858_San_Diego_hurricane" title="1858 San Diego hurricane">hurricane</a> makes a direct hit on Southern California before dissipating. <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a> experienced hurricane-force winds with torrential rainfall recorded all across Southern California.</li>\n<li><b>After October or before June, 1859</b>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 A system considered a tropical cyclone makes landfall between <a href="/wiki/Cape_Mendocino" title="Cape Mendocino">Cape Mendocino</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay" title="San Francisco Bay">San Francisco Bay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Visher_p296_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Visher_p296-60">[60]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>September 25, 1939</b>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 The <a href="/wiki/1939_California_tropical_storm" title="1939 California tropical storm">1939 California tropical storm</a> makes landfall in California, killing 45<sup id="cite_ref-Hurd_1939_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hurd_1939-99">[99]</a></sup> to 93.<sup id="cite_ref-history_of_sig_events_p14_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history_of_sig_events_p14-100">[100]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>September 6, 1972</b>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/1972_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Hyacinth" title="1972 Pacific hurricane season">Tropical Depression Hyacinth</a> makes landfall.<sup id="cite_ref-Unisys_Hyacinth_1972_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unisys_Hyacinth_1972-101">[101]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>September 6, 1978</b>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Norman_(1978)" title="Hurricane Norman (1978)">Tropical Depression Norman</a> makes landfall.<sup id="cite_ref-Unisys_Norman_1978_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unisys_Norman_1978-102">[102]</a></sup></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span 1992</b>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Iniki" title="Hurricane Iniki">Hurricane Iniki</a> makes landfall on <a href="/wiki/Kauai" title="Kauai">Kauai</a>, killing six throughout the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-CPHC_1992_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPHC_1992-44">[44]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>September 14, 1992</b>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 <a id="cite_ref-HPC_Norma_1981_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HPC_Norma_1981-126">[126]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Worldwide_cyclone_records_set_by_Pacific_storms">Worldwide cyclone records set by Pacific storms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Worldwide cyclone records set by Pacific storms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul>\n<li><b>Highest official wind speed ever recorded in a tropical cyclone</b>: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Patricia" title="Hurricane Patricia">Hurricane Patricia</a> with maximum sustained winds of 215&#160;mph (345&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-D14_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D14-135">[135]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Fastest intensification (1-minute sustained surface <a href="/wiki/Wind" title="Wind">winds</a>)</b>: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Patricia" title="Hurricane Patricia">Hurricane Patricia</a> 55 <a href="/wiki/Metre_per_second" title="Metre per second">m/s</a> (120&#160;mph, 105 <a href="/wiki/Knot_(unit)" title="Knot (unit)">kt</a>, 195&#160;km/h), from 40 <a href="/wiki/Metre_per_second" title="Metre per second">m/s</a> (85&#160;mph, 75 <a href="/wiki/Knot_(unit)" title="Knot (unit)">kt</a>, 140&#160;km/h) to 95 <a href="/wiki/Metre_per_second" title="Metre per second">m/s</a> (205&#160;mph, 180 <a href="/wiki/Knot_(unit)" title="Knot (unit)">kt</a>, 335&#160;km/h) in under 24 h<sup id="cite_ref-TCR1_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR1-136">[136]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Warmest eye in a tropical cyclone</b>: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Patricia" title="Hurricane Patricia">Hurricane Patricia</a> 32.2&#160;\xc2\xb0C (90.0&#160;\xc2\xb0F) at 758 hPa height.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Longest-lived tropical cyclone</b>: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_John_(1994)" title="Hurricane John (1994)">Hurricane John</a> lasted for 30&#160;days and 18&#160;hours.<sup id="cite_ref-tc_records_CPHC_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tc_records_CPHC-48">[48]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Farthest-travelling tropical cyclone</b>: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_John_(1994)" title="Hurricane John (1994)">Hurricane John</a> travelled for 13,280&#160;km.<sup id="cite_ref-tc_records_CPHC_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tc_records_CPHC-48">[48]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Highest <a href="/wiki/Accumulated_cyclone_energy" title="Accumulated cyclone energy">Accumulated cyclone energy (ACE)</a> index for a tropical cyclone</b>: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ioke" title="Hurricane Ioke">Hurricane/Typhoon Ioke</a> achieved an ACE index of 82.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Tropical cyclone at Category&#160;4 or 5 intensity on the <a href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir-Simpson Scale</a> for the longest</b>: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ioke" title="Hurricane Ioke">Hurricane Ioke</a> was at that intensity for 198 consecutive hours.<sup id="cite_ref-CPHC_2006_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPHC_2006-88">[88]</a></sup></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
